[(Brahman.тАФ─Бdhy─Бtmam; rohit─Бdityadevatyam. tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham:) 1, 12-15, 39-41. anuс╣гс╣нubh; 2, 3, 8, 43. jagat─л; 10. ─Бst─Бrapan╠Дkti; 11. bс╣Ыhat─лgarbh─Б; 16-24. ─Бrс╣г─л g─Бyatr─л; 25. kakummaty ─Бst─Бrapan╠Дkti; 26. purodvyatij─Бgat─Б bhurig jagat─л; 27. vir─Бс╕Н jagat─л; 29. b─Бrhatagarbh─Б тАШnuс╣гс╣нubh; 30. 5-p. uс╣гс╣Зigbс╣Ыhat─лgarbh─Б тАШtijagat─л; 34. ─Бrс╣г─л pan╠Дkti; 37. 5-p. vir─Бс╕Нgarbh─Б jagat─л; 44, 45. jagat─л (44. 4-p. puraс╕е┼Ы─Бkvar─Б bhurij; 45. atij─Бgatagarbh─Б).]

Whitney

Comment

Found also in P─Бipp. xviii. Only twice (vs. 1) quoted in K─Бu┼Ы., but several times (eight different verses) by V─Бit.

Translations

Translated: Ludwig, p. 540; Henry, 8, 36; Griffith, ii. 143.тАФIn this hymn, the sun is mentioned by the name r├│hita only in vss. 25 and 39-41. Verses 39-41 are translated also by Muir, v. 396; Scherman, p. 75 (with vss. 25-26); Deussen, Geschichte, i. 1. 213 (also vss. 25-26 at p. 226).тАФThe verses 16-24, which are RV. i. 50. 1-9, are translated by the RV. translators, and are commented and in part translated by me in Skt. Reader, p. 362-3.

Griffith

The glorification of the Sun as Aditya, Surya and Rohita

Translation
  1. The bright (┼Ыukr├б) shining lights (ket├║) of him go up in the
    skyтАФof the men-watching Aditya, him of great courses (-vrat├б), liberal
    (m─лс╕Нhv─Б╠Бс╣Еs).
Notes

Ppp. reads in d mah─лvr-. K─Бu┼Ы. 58. 22 prescribes the use
apparently of the whole hymn (with xvi. 3 and xvii.) in an act of
worship to the rising sun, in a ceremony for long life; also (with the
same and other hymns, and xiii. 1. 25) in 18. 25, in the citr─Бkarman:
see the note to 1. 25 above. V─Бit. 9. 16 uses it in the c─Бturm─Бsya
ceremony when turning toward the sun in the east.

Griffith

Radiant, refulgent in the sky are reared the banners of his light, Aditya’s, who beholdeth man, mighty in act and bountiful.

Whitney
Translation
  1. [Him,] shining (svar) with the brightness (arc├нs) of the
    foreknowing quarters, well-winged, flying swift in the ocean
    (arс╣Зav├б)тАФwe would praise the sun, the shepherd of existence, who with
    his rays shines unto all the quarters.
Notes

The Pet. Lex. (followed by Henry) emends praj├▒─Б╠Бn─Бm to praj├▒─Б╠Бnam,
with much plausibility; yet it is opposed by x. 7. 34, d├н┼Ыo y├б┼Ы cakr├й
praj├▒─Б╠Бn─лс╕е. Ppp. reads praj├▒─Бnaс╣Б svadayanto arc-; and it combines in
d di┼Ы─Б тАЭbh─Бti. The verse lacks two syllables of being a proper
jagat─л.

Griffith

Let us laud him, the whole world’s Herdsman, Surya, who with his rays illumines all the regions, Mark of the quarters, brightening them with lustre, swift, mighty-pinioned, flying in the ocean.

Whitney
Translation
  1. In that thou goest swiftly eastward, westward, at will (svadh├бy─Б),
    makest by magic (m─Бy─Б╠Б) the two days of diverse formтАФthat, O ─Аditya,
    [is] great, that thy great fame (┼Ыr─Б╠Бvas), that thou alone art born
    about the whole world (bh┼л╠Бman).
Notes

‘The two days,’ i.e. ‘day and night’ The first p─Бda is triс╣гс╣нubh.

Griffith

From west to east thou speedest freely, making by magic day and night of diverse colours. This is Aditya, thy transcendent glory, that thou alone art born through all creation.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The inspired, hasting (tar├бс╣Зi), shining one, whom seven numerous
    (bah├║) yellow steeds (har├нt) draw, whom out of the liquid (?
    srut├б) Atri conducted up the skyтАФthee here they see going around upon
    thy race.
Notes

Half of our mss. appear plainly to read stut─Б╠Бt in c, but the
apparent distinction is of no value; sr and st are virtually one in
ms. use. Ppp. helps to establish sru-, by reading, for c, d,
┼Ыrut─Бd divam atri divam anyan─Бya taс╣Б tv─Б pa┼Ыyema paryajitim ─Бjim. GB.
i. 2. 17 has c (the published text reads stut─Бd), with vs. 12 a,
b, as if a verse. тМКAs for the Atri story, cf. my essay on RV. v. 40 in
Festgruss an Roth, p. 187. For the construction of ─Бj├нm, see Ved.

Griffith

Victorious, inspired, and brightly shining, whom seven strong tawny-coloured coursers carry, Whom Atri lifted from the flood to heaven, thus men behold thee as thy course thou runnest.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрдореН) рдЬрд┐рд╕ (рд╡рд┐рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддрдореН) рд╡рд┐рд╡рд┐рдз рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ [рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐рд╡ рд░рд╕] рдПрдХрддреНрд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рднреНрд░рд╛рдЬрдорд╛рдирдореН) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рди, (рддрд░рдгрд┐рдореН) [рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░ рд╕реЗ] рдкрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдХреЛ (рд╕рдкреНрдд) рд╕рд╛рдд [рд╢реБрдХреНрд▓, рдиреАрд▓, рдкреАрдд, рд░рдХреНрдд, рд╣рд░рд┐рдд, рдХрдкрд┐рд╢, рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░ рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╡рд╛рд▓реА] (рдмрд╣реНрд╡реАрдГ) рдмрд╣реБрдд [рднрд┐рдиреНрди-рднрд┐рдиреНрди рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рд╡рд╛рд▓реА] (рд╣рд░рд┐рддрдГ) рдЖрдХрд░реНрд╖рдХ рдХрд┐рд░рдгреЗрдВ (рд╡рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐) рд▓реЗ рдЪрд▓рддреА рд╣реИрдВред (рдпрдореН) рдЬрд┐рд╕ [рд╕реВрд░реНрдп] рдХреЛ (рдЕрддреНрд░рд┐рдГ) рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреА [рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛] рдиреЗ (рд╕реНрд░реБрддрд╛рддреН) рдмрд╣рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП [рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рд░реВрдк рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░] рд╕реЗ (рджрд┐рд╡рдореН) рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ рдореЗрдВ (рдЙрдиреНрдирд┐рдирд╛рдп) рдКрдБрдЪрд╛ рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ, (рддрдореН рддреНрд╡рд╛) рдЙрд╕реЗ рддреБрдЭ [рд╕реВрд░реНрдп] рдХреЛ (рдЖрдЬрд┐рдореН) рдорд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд╛ рдкрд░ (рдкрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдиреНрддрдореН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдерд╛ рдЪрд▓рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ (рдкрд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐) рд╡реЗ [рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН] рджреЗрдЦрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реерекрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

режрел рдорд╛ рддреНрд╡рд╛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. Let them not damage thee going around upon thy race; happily do thou
    cross the difficulties quickly; when, O sun, thou goest to both sky and
    divine earth, measuring out day-and-night.
Notes

Or, ‘sky’ and ’earth’ may be joint objects of ‘measuring’ (so Henry, and
apparently Ludwig). Ppp. reads paryantam in a, and sugena durgam
in b. We have to make the, in its situation, awkward resolution
tu-─Б in a in order to fill out the meter; тМКor -y─Бantam?тМЛ.

Griffith

Let them not snare thee speeding on thy journey: pass safely, swiftly places hard to traverse, While measuring out the day and night thou movest–O Surya, even Heaven and Earth the Goddess.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Well-being, O sun, [be] to thy chariot for its moving, wherewith
    thou goest at once about both borders (├бnta)тАФwhich thy yellow steeds,
    of excellent draught, draw: a hundred horses, or else seven, numerous.
Notes

‘At once’ (sady├бs), doubtless ‘on one and the same day’; ‘borders,’
i.e. ‘horizons.’ Half the mss. read b├бhiс╣гс╣нh─Бs, both in this and in the
next verse. Ppp. has in a carato rath─Бsi, and in b
pary─Бsi;* and for d, instead of repeating 7 d, it gives tam
─Б roha sukham ─Бsy a┼Ыvam. тМК“Numerous” is fem.; and we may think of
“horses” as fem.тМЛ *тМКFor the relation of pariy─Бsi to pary─Бsi, cf.
that of -─Бni yasya to -─Бс╣Еsy asya, above, x. 7. 20, and see Gram.

Griffith

Hail to thy rapid car whereon, O Surya, thou circlest in a moment both the limits, Whirled by thy bay steeds, best of all at drawing, thy hundred horses or seven goodly coursers!

Whitney
Translation
  1. The sun hath yoked in his chariot, in order to go, his seven great
    yellow steeds, golden-skinned; the bright one hath been freed from the
    dimness (? r├бjas) in the distance; shaking away the darkness, the god
    hath mounted the sky.
Notes

Ppp. reads ┼Ы┼лras for s┼лryas in a, and ┼Ыakras for ┼Ыukras in
c, and apparently ayun╠Дkta in b. The verse is very ill defined
as simple jagat─л; the true reading in b would seem to be
h├нraс╣Зyatvacas.

Griffith

Surya hath harnessed to his car to draw him seven stately bay steeds gay with wolden housings. The Bright One started from the distant region: dispelling gloom the God hath climbed the heavens.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The god hath come up with great show (ket├║); he hath wasted away
    the darkness, hath set up (abhi-┼Ыri) the light; that hero, heavenly
    eagle, son of Aditi, hath looked abroad unto all beings.
Notes

Abhi-┼Ыri, more literally, ‘affix, fasten on’ (to the sky). тМКFor the
form a┼Ыr─Бit, see Gram. ┬з 889 a, and note to vi. 32. 2. For avс╣Ыk,
Gram. ┬з 832 a.тМЛ Ppp. reads in c sthaviras for sa v─лras, and
has a curious d: ─Бdity─Бс╣г putraс╣Б n─Бthag─Бm abhay─Бm at─лt─Б.

Griffith

With lofty banner hath the God gone upward, and introduced the light, expelling darkness. He hath looked round on all the worlds, the Hero, the son of Aditi, Celestial Eagle.

Rising, thou spreadest out thy rays, thou nourishest all shapes and forms. Thou with thy power illumest both the oceans, encompassing all spheres with thy refulgence.

резрез рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдкрд░рдВ рдЪрд░рддреЛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. They two move on one after the other by magic; two playing young
    ones go about the ocean; the one looks abroad upon all beings; yellow
    steeds draw the other with golden [trappings?].
Notes

The first three p─Бdas are identical with vii. 81. 1 a-c (repeated at
xiv. 1. 23), and are found in other texts: see the note to that verse;
the last p─Бda is peculiar, and, as applying only to the sun, spoils the
description of the pair of luminaries, sun and moon, which the verse
sets out to make. Henry regards the daily and the nightly sun as
intended, and the h─Бiraс╣Зyas as the stars, by means of which the latter
finds his way back to the eastern horizon. It would have been better to
read y─Бto тАШrс╣Зav├бm here, as in vii. 81. 1, since the majority of our
saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. (all save Bs.E.) give it in this place also.

Griffith

Moving by magic power to east and westward, these two young creatures, sporting, circle ocean. One of the pair beholds all living creatures: with wheels of gold the bay steeds bear the other.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдПрддреМ) рдпрд╣ рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ [рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╛] (рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рдкрд░рдореН) рдЖрдЧреЗ-рдкреАрдЫреЗ (рдорд╛рдпрдпрд╛) рдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐ рд╕реЗ [рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдирд┐рдпрдо рд╕реЗ] (рдЪрд░рддрдГ) рд╡рд┐рдЪрд░рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, (рдХреНрд░реАрдбрдиреНрддреМ) рдЦреЗрд▓рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рд╢рд┐рд╢реВ) рджреЛ рдмрд╛рд▓рдХ [рдЬреИрд╕реЗ] (рдЕрд░реНрдгрд╡рдореН) рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖ рдореЗрдВ (рдкрд░рд┐) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ (рдпрд╛рддрдГ) рдЪрд▓рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВред (рдЕрдиреНрдпрдГ) рдПрдХ [рд╕реВрд░реНрдп] (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛) рд╕рдм (рднреБрд╡рдирд╛) рднреБрд╡рдиреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╖реНрдЯреЗ) рджреЗрдЦрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, (рдЕрдиреНрдпрдореН) рджреВрд╕рд░реЗ [рдЪрдиреНрджреНрд░рдорд╛] рдХреЛ (рд╣рд░рд┐рддрдГ) [рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдХреА] рдЖрдХрд░реНрд╖рдХ рдХрд┐рд░рдгреЗрдВ (рд╣реИрд░рдгреНрдпреИрдГ) рддреЗрдЬреЛрдордп [рд╡рд╛ рд╕реБрдиреИрд▓реЗ] рдХрд╛рдореЛрдВ рдХреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд░рд╛ (рд╡рд╣рдиреНрддрд┐) рд▓реЗ рдЪрд▓рддреА рд╣реИрдВ реерезрезрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Translation
  1. That one he attains completely (sam-─Бp) with his swiftnesses;
    that he desires not to neglect (? apa-cikits); by that [men] do not

Apa-cikits, lit. ‘desire to think away from,’ with abl.; the
expression is found only here. The logic of d is not obvious; Henry
supplies ’the demons’ as subject of ├бva rundhate; Ludwig renders it as
a singular. Ppp. reads jigitsati in b; and, in c etc.,
bhakс╣гaс╣Зaс╣Б dev─Бn─Бn naс╣Б va ru-; bhakс╣гaс╣Зam is an improvement; the meter
of c halts badly without it.

Griffith

He finishes his race with speed and never turns his thought aside, Thereby he keeps not from the Gods enjoyment of the Drink of Life.

Translation
  1. This heavenly J─Бtavedas the lights (ket├║) draw (vah) up, for
    every one to see the sun.
Notes

Or s┼л╠Бryam may be in apposition with j─Бt├бvedasam. ‘Draw,’ i.e. as
horses do. This verse, with the eight that follow, constitute RV. i. 50.
1-9, in the same order of verses, and with few variants; they are also
all found in one or more other Vedic texts: this one in SV. (i. 31), VS.
(7. 41; 8. 41; 33. 31), TS. (i. 2. 8┬▓; 4. 43┬╣), and MS. (i. 3. 37)тАФin
all, without a variant. The whole hymn тМКi.e. vss. 16-24тМЛ is repeated
further in xx. 47. 13-21. This verse is used three times in V─Бit.: at
21. 23; at 33. 5 (with the following five verses); and at 39. 16 (with
the following two verses). тМКThe prat─лka is cited at MGS. i. 2. 4. The
frequency of the citation or occurrence of the verse may be judged by
consulting MGS. Index, p. 148.тМЛ

Griffith

His heralds bear him up aloft, the God who knoweth all that live, Surya, that all may look on him.

Griffith

His herald rays are seen afar refulgent o’er the world of men, Like flames of fire that burn and blaze.

Whitney
Translation
  1. In front of the clans of the gods, in front of those of men thou
    risest; in front of every one, for seeing the sky (sv├аr).
Notes

RV. reads at end of b m─Б╠Бnuс╣г─Бn, and SV. (i. 637) has the same.

Griffith

Thou goest to the hosts of Gods, thou comest hither to mankind, Hither, all light to behold.

Griffith

Surya, hath yoked the pure bright seven, the daughters of the car, with these, His own dear team, he travelleth.

    over-lord of the gods.
Notes

Ppp. reads in a ─Б тАЩkram─лt. The Anukr. regards the verse as one of
four p─Бdas (8 + 6: 12 + 11); but the first two are plainly one
triс╣гс╣нubh p─Бda, with t├бpas─Б intruded into it. Rohita appears here
for the first time in this second hymn, instead of simply the sun; nor
do we meet him elsewhere, save in vss. 39-41.

Griffith

Devout, aflame with fervent heat, Rohita hath gone up to heaven. He is re-born, returning to his birthplace, and hath become the Gods’ imperial ruler.

Whitney
Translation
  1. He who belongs to all men (-carс╣гaс╣З├н) and has faces on all sides,
    who has hands on all sides and palms on all sidesтАФhe brings together
    with his (two) arms, together with his wings (pl.), generating
    heaven-and-earth, sole god.
Notes

The verse is, with considerable variations, RV. x. 81. 3, found also in
VS. (xvii. 19: same text as RV.), TS. (iv. 6. 2тБ┤), TA. (x. 1. 3), and
MS. (ii. 10. 2). None of the other texts has y├бs in b, and only
MS. in a; they begin vi┼Ыv├бta┼Ыc─Бkс╣гur (but MS. y├│ vi┼Ыv├бcakс╣гur); in
b, RV.VS. begin with vi┼Ыv├бtob─Бhur, TS.TA.MS. -hasta, and all end
with vi┼Ыv├бtasp─Бt; in c, for bh├бrati, RV. (and VS.) has
dh├бmati, TS.TA. n├бmati, MS. ├бdhamat; in d, RV.VS.MS. give
dy─Б╠Бv─Бbh┼л╠Бm─л. Ppp. agrees with RV. in b-d. The meter, fairly regular
in RV., is distorted greatly in our text (13 + 13: 11 + 12 = 49); the
Anukr. gives an acceptable definition of it. The sense also is much
defaced in the first line as we have it. V─Бit. 29. 14 uses the verse to
accompany a certain graha in the building of the fire-altar.

Griffith

Dear unto all men, facing all directions, with hands and palms on every side extended, He, the sole God, engendering earth and heaven, beareth them with his wings and arms together.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрдГ) рдЬреЛ [рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░] (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдЪрд░реНрд╖рдгрд┐рдГ) рд╕рдмрдХрд╛ рджреЗрдЦрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛, (рдЙрдд) рдФрд░ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рддреЛрдореБрдЦрдГ) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ рдореБрдЦ [рдореБрдЦреНрдп рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рд╡рд╛ рдЙрдкрд╛рдп] рд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛, (рдпрдГ) рдЬреЛ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рддрд╕реНрдкрд╛рдгрд┐рдГ) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ рд╣рд╛рде рдХреЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛, (рдЙрдд) рдФрд░ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рддрд╕реНрдкреГрдердГ) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ рдкреВрд░реНрддрд┐рд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╣реИред (рдПрдХрдГ) рд╡рд╣ рдЕрдХреЗрд▓рд╛ (рджреЗрд╡рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк [рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛] (рдмрд╛рд╣реБрднреНрдпрд╛рдореН) рджреЛрдиреЛрдВ [рдзрд╛рд░рдг-рдЖрдХрд░реНрд╖рдг рд░реВрдк] рднреБрдЬрд╛рдУрдВ рд╕реЗ (рдкрддрддреНрд░реИрдГ рд╕рдореН) рдЧрдордирд╢реАрд▓ рдкрд░рдорд╛рдгреБрдУрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде (рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА) рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реА рдХреЛ (рдЬрдирдпрдиреН) рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ (рд╕рдореН) рдпрдерд╛рд╡рддреН (рднрд░рддрд┐) рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ реереиремрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Whitney
Translation
  1. The one-footed strode out more than the two-footed; the two-footed
    falls upon (abhi-i) the three-footed from behind; the two-footed
    strode out more than the six-footed; they sit together [about] the
    body of the one-footed.
Notes

Sam-─Бs has no good right to an accusative object; and one of our mss.
(D.) reads tanv├аm, loc, which would be grammatically an acceptable
emendation; as regards the sense, that is too obscure for us to derive
any help from it. P─Бdas b and c are wanting in Ppp., probably
by accident. The first half-verse nearly agrees with RV. x. 117. 8 a,
b, which (whole) verse corresponds to тМКthe first half ofтМЛ our 3. 25
below: see the note there. It is only here and in 3. 25 that we find the
accentuation dv├нp─Бt and tr├нp─Бt. тМКThe prat─лka is quoted by GB. ii.
9, p. 28, l. 19.тМЛ The description of the Anukr. implies an unfounded
rejection of one of the resolutions abh├н eti or tan├║-am.

Griffith

The single-footed hath outstepped the biped, the biped overtakes the triple-footed. The biped hath outstridden the six-footed: these sit around the single-footed’s body.

рдПрдХреСрд╜рдкрд╛рддреНред рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╜рдкреСрджрдГред рднреВрдпрдГреСред рд╡рд┐ред рдЪреТрдХреНрд░реТрдореЗреТред рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╜рдкрд╛реСрддреНред рддреНрд░рд┐рд╜рдкрд╛реСрджрдореНред рдЕреТрднрд┐ред рдПреТрддрд┐реТред рдкреТрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рддреНред рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╜рдкрд╛реСрддреНред рд╣реТред рд╖рдЯреНрд╜рдкреСрджрдГред рднреВрдпрдГреСред рд╡рд┐ред рдЪреТрдХреНрд░реТрдореЗреТред рддреЗред рдПрдХреСрд╜рдкрджрдГред рддреТрдиреНрд╡с│брдореНред рд╕рдореНред рдЖреТрд╕реТрддреЗреТред реи.реиренред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдПрдХрдкрд╛рддреН) рдПрдХрд░рд╕ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ (рджреНрд╡рд┐рдкрджрдГ) рджреЛ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдХреА рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд┐рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ [рдЬрдЩреНрдЧрдо рд╕реНрдерд╛рд╡рд░ рдЬрдЧрддреН] рд╕реЗ (рднреВрдпрдГ) рдЕрдзрд┐рдХ рдЖрдЧреЗ (рд╡рд┐) рдлреИрд▓рдХрд░ (рдЪрдХреНрд░рдореЗ) рдЪрд▓рд╛ рдЧрдпрд╛, (рджреНрд╡рд┐рдкрд╛рджреН) рджреЛ [рднреВрдд рднрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддреН] рдореЗрдВ рдЧрддрд┐рд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ (рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рддреН) рдлрд┐рд░ (рддреНрд░рд┐рдкрд╛рджрдореН) рддреАрди [рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рди рдФрд░ рдЕрдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рди рдФрд░ рдордзреНрдп рд▓реЛрдХреЛрдВ] рдореЗрдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕рдВрд╕рд╛рд░ рдореЗрдВ (рдЕрднрд┐) рд╕рдм рдУрд░ рд╕реЗ (рдПрддрд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, (рджреНрд╡рд┐рдкрд╛рддреН) рджреЛ [рдЬрдЩреНрдЧрдо рдФрд░ рд╕реНрдерд╛рд╡рд░ рдЬрдЧрддреН] рдореЗрдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░ (рд╣) рдирд┐рд╢реНрдЪрдп рдХрд░рдХреЗ (рд╖рдЯреНрдкрджрдГ) рдЫрд╣ [рдкреВрд░реНрд╡ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдг рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдо рдЙрддреНрддрд░ рдКрдБрдЪреА рдФрд░ рдиреАрдЪреА рджрд┐рд╢рд╛рдУрдВ] рдореЗрдВ рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд┐рд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдгреНрдб рд╕реЗ (рднреВрдпрдГ) рдЕрдзрд┐рдХ рдЖрдЧреЗ (рд╡рд┐рдЪрдХреНрд░рдореЗ) рдирд┐рдХрд▓ рдЧрдпрд╛, (рддреЗ) рд╡реЗ [рдпреЛрдЧреА рдЬрди] (рдПрдХрдкрджрдГ) рдПрдХрд░рд╕ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдХреА (рддрдиреНрд╡рдореН) рдЙрдкрдХрд╛рд░ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛ рдХреЛ (рд╕рдореН) рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ (рдЖрд╕рддреЗ) рд╕реЗрд╡рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реереиренрее

Translation
  1. When, about to go unwearied, he hath approached (─Б-sth─Б) his
    yellow steeds, he, shining (ruc), makes for himself two forms; rising
    rich in lights (ket├║-), overpowering the dim spaces (r├бjas), thou
    illuminest (vi-bh─Б), O ─Аditya, all the advances.

Griffith

When he, unwearied, fain to go, hath mounted his bays, he makes two colours, brightly shining. Rising with banners, conquering the regions, thou sendest light through all the floods, Aditya.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Verily (b├бс╣н), great art thou, O sun; verily, O ─Аditya, great art
    thou; great is the greatness of thee the great one; thou, O ─Аditya, art
    great.
Notes

This verse is RV. viii. 90 (or 101). 11, and is found also in VS.
(xxxiii. 39) and SV. (i. 276; ii. 1138), while its prat─лka is given by
TB. (i. 4. 5┬│: very strange, since the whole verse occurs in no
T─Бittir─лya text). RV. and VS. read, for c, d, mah├бs te sat├│ mahim─Б╠Б
panasyate тАШddh─Б╠Б deva mah─Б╠Бс╣Е asi; тМКthe vs. is repeated in RV. form at xx.
58. 3;тМЛ and SV. the same, except paniс╣гс╣нama mahn─Б╠Б for panasyate
тАШddh─Б╠Б.

Griffith

Verily, Surya, thou art great: truly, Aditya, thou art great. Great is thy grandeur, Mighty One: thou, O Aditya, thou art great.

Translation
  1. Thou shinest (ruc) in the sky, thou shinest in the atmosphere, O
    flying one; on the earth thou shinest, thou shinest within the waters;
    both oceans thou hast penetrated (vi-─Бp) with thy sheen (r├║ci); a
    god, O god, art thou, a heaven-conquering bull (mahiс╣г├б).
Notes

Ppp. reads at the end svarvit. The Anukr. understands the structure of
the verse as 12 + 9 + 7: 12 + 11 = 51; but it is plainly a mixed
triс╣гс╣нubh-jagat─л, rather, with patan╠Дga intruded at the end of a,
and possibly one r├│case in b. All the mss. accent patan╠Дga,
because they reckon it, with the Anukr., as first word in a p─Бda; it
should properly be patan╠Дga.

Griffith

In heaven, O Bird, and in mid-air thou shinest: thou shinest on the earth and in the waters. Thou hast pervaded both the seas with splendour: a God art thou, O God, light-winner, mighty.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Wondrous, understanding (cikitv─Бс╣Еs), a bull (mahiс╣г├б), an eagle,
    making to shine the two firmaments (r├│das─л), the
    atmosphereтАФday-and-night, clothing themselves about with the sun,
    lengthen out all his heroisms.
Notes

The adjectives in a, b are nom. masc. sing., and the shift of
construction in the second half-verse is a notable one. Ppp. combines
suparс╣З─Б тАЭroc-, and reads rodas─лm in b. The verse is used in
V─Бit. 33. 8 in a sacrificial session, with the remaining verses to the
end of the hymn. Ppp. puts our vs. 33 before this. тМКThe first p─Бda is
nearly the same as 42 c.тМЛ тМКHenry discusses the vs. in M├йm. de la
Soc. de linguistique, x. 86.тМЛ

Griffith

Brilliant, observant, mighty Lord, an Eagle illuming both the spheres and air between them. Day and the Night, clad in the robes of Surya, spread forth more widely all his hero powers.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Keen (tigm├б), shining out (vi-bhr─Бj), sharpening himself,
    granting the helpful (? araс╣Бgam├б) advances, a winged one full of
    light, a vigor-bestowing bull (mahiс╣г├б), he hath approached (─Б-sth─Б)
    all the directions, arranging (kс╕╖p).

Griffith

Flaming and radiant, strengthening his body, bestowing floods that promptly come to meet us, He, luminous, winged, mighty, strength-bestower, hath mounted all the regions as he forms them.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Wondrous front [and] show (ket├║) of the gods, the sun, full of
    light, going up the directions (prad├н┼Ы), the day-maker, bright
    (┼Ыukr├б), hath overpassed with brightnesses (dyumn├б) the glooms
    (t├бmas) [and] all difficulties.
Notes

This verse and the next are repeated as xx. 107. 13, 14. The definition
of this one by the Anukr. тМКas 40 syllables is right from its point of
view; but the verseтМЛ is evidently meant for a triс╣гс╣нubh, and can easily
be read into a respectable one, according to the low standard of AV.
triс╣гс╣нubhs, by a few judicious resolutions. The harshness and obscurity
of the constructions in a, b are indications of a corrupted text;
Henry renders prad├н┼Ыas by ’toward the celestial regions,’ Ludwig by
‘from the horizon’; the translation above simply adheres to the usual
sense of the word. Verses 34-36 are directed in V─Бit. 39. 16 to be used
alternatively in the praise of the sun; in 21. 23, the prat─лka, namely
citraс╣Б dev─Бn─Бm (quoted with vs. 16), might apply either to this verse
or to the next.

Griffith

Bright presence of the Gods, the luminous herald Surya hath mounted the celestial regions. Day’s maker, he hath shone away the darkness, and radiant, passed o’er places hard to traverse.

    Varuс╣Зa, of Agni; he hath filled heaven-and-earth, the atmosphere; the
    sun is the soul of the moving creation (j├бgat) and of the stationary
    (tasthiv─Б╠Бс╣Еs).

found almost everywhere else: thus, in SV. (i. 630: N─Бigeya appendix),

TA. (i. 7. 6; ii. 13. 1), MS. (i. 3. 37), AA. (iii. 2. 3); all have the
same text as RV.; and so, apparently, has Ppp., тМКcombining, however,
─Бpr─Бdy─Б-тМЛ. тМКDeussen, Geschichte, i. 1. 213, interprets the vs.тМЛ The
quotation in V─Бit. 33. 6 evidently applies to the verse as AV. xx. 107.
14. тМКin d, j├бgas tas- is a misprint for j├бgatas tas-: an
interesting instance of most modern haplography.тМЛ

Translation
  1. Flying on high (ucc─Б╠Б), the red eagle, in the midst of the sky
    hasting, shiningтАФmay we see thee, whom men call the impeller (savitс╣Ы╠Б),
    the unfailing light which Atri found.

Griffith

High in the midst of heaven may we behold thee whom men call Savitar, the bright red Eagle, Soaring and speeding on thy way, refulgent, unwasting light which Atri erst discovered.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЙрдЪреНрдЪрд╛) рдКрдБрдЪреЗ (рдкрддрдиреНрддрдореН) рдРрд╢реНрд╡рд░реНрдпрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реБрдП, (рдЕрд░реБрдгрдореН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ, (рд╕реБрдкрд░реНрдгрдореН) рдмрдбрд╝реЗ рдкрд╛рд▓рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ, (рджрд┐рд╡рдГ) рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░ рдХреЗ (рдордзреНрдпреЗ) рдордзреНрдп (рддрд░рдгрд┐рдореН) рдкрд╛рд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ (рднреНрд░рд╛рдЬрдорд╛рдирдореН) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рди, (рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛рд░рдореН) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдХ (рддреНрд╡рд╛) рддреБрдЭ [рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░] рдХреЛ (рдкрд╢реНрдпрд╛рдо) рд╣рдо рджреЗрдЦреЗрдВ, (рдпрдореН) рдЬрд┐рд╕рдХреЛ (рдЕрдЬрд╕реНрд░рдореН) рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ (рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рдГ) рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐ (рдЖрд╣реБрдГ) рд╡реЗ [рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд▓реЛрдЧ] рдмрддрд╛рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, (рдпрддреН) рдЬрд┐рд╕ [рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐] рдХреЛ (рдЕрддреНрддреНрд░рд┐рдГ) рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдиреА [рдпреЛрдЧреА рдкреБрд░реБрд╖] рдиреЗ (рдЕрд╡рд┐рдиреНрджрддреН) рдкрд╛рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ реерейремрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Whitney
Translation
  1. To the eagle running on the back of the sky, to the son of Aditi, I,
    frightened, approach (upa-y─Б), desiring refuge; do thou, O sun,
    lengthen out for us a long life-time; may we take no harm; may we be in
    thy favor.
Notes

The verse is obviously a regular triс╣гс╣нubh, with n─Бth├бk─Бmas intruded
in b: its description by the Anukr. тМКgives the verse 48 syllables;
but how pa├▒capad─Б vir─Бс╕Нgarbh─Б is to be understood is not clearтМЛ. тМКThe
verse is quoted in V─Бit. 18. 7, in the agniс╣гс╣нoma.тМЛ

Griffith

Him, Son of Aditi, an Eagle hasting along heaven’s height, I supplicate in terror, As such prolong our lengthened life, O Surya: may we, unha- rmed, enjoy thy gracious favour.

  1. A thousand days’ journey are expanded the wings of him, of the
    yellow swan flying to heaven; he, putting all the gods in his breast,
    goes viewing together all existences.
Notes

We had the verse above as x. 8. 18, and it is repeated again below as 3.
14. Ppp. reads in c sa vicv─Бn dev─Бn.

Griffith

This gold-hued Hansa’s wings, soaring to heaven, spread o’er a thousand days’ continued journey Supporting all the Gods upon his bosom, he goes his way behold- ing every creature.

Translation
  1. The ruddy one became time, the ruddy one in the beginning Praj─Бpati;
    the ruddy one [is] face (mouth?) of the sacrifices; the ruddy one
    brought the bright sky (sv├аr).
Notes

Ppp. reads in a loko тАШbhavat (our 40 a), and, for d,
rohito jyotir ucyate.

Griffith

Rohita, in primeval days Prajapati, was, after, Time, Mouth of all sacrifices, he, Rohita, brought celestial light.

Whitney
Translation
  1. He, mounting, glowing [and] unwearied, the great [spaces], makes
    for himself, shining (ruc), two forms; wondrous, understanding,
    тМКbull,тМЛ wind-going (??), when he shines out (vi-bh─Б) upon as many
    worlds [as there are].
Notes

That is, ‘upon all existing worlds.’ The second p─Бda is 28 b above;
the third, nearly 32 a. The rendering of v─Бtam─Бy─Бs (p.
v─Б╠Бtamре░─Бy─Бс╕е) in c is purely to fill up the text. Henry emends to
v─Б╠Бtam ─Б╠Бpas; Ludwig renders ‘possessing wind-magic’ The Anukr. passes
without notice the redundant syllable in c. Ppp. has a quite
different version of much of the verse: ─Бrohan chakro vс╣Ыhat─лr yuс╣Бktor
amarty─Бс╣г kс╣Ыс╣Зuс╣гe v─лry─Бni: divyas suparс╣Зo muhiс╣гaс╣Б v─Бtaraс╣Еh─Бya: sarv─Бс╣Еl
lok─Бс╣Е abhi etc. This would suggest v─Бtaraс╣Еh─Бs ‘wind-swift’ as
emendation of v─Бtam─Бy─Бs.

Griffith

Mounting the lofty ones, he, bright, unwearied, splendidly shining, makes two separate colours, While through all worlds that are he sends his lustre, radiant, observant, mighty, wind-approacher.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The one he falls upon (abhi-i), the other he casts aboutтАФthe bull,
    arranging with day-and-night; we, imploring, call upon the track-finding
    sun, dwelling in the welkin (r├бjas).
Notes

In the very obscure first half-verse, the two anyat’s may be subjects
instead (so Ludwig and Henry), asyate being taken as passiveтАФwhich
would seem more natural, save that then the nominative in b is left
without construction. Ppp. reads in a-b eti sadyo тАШyaс╣Б vas─Бvam
aho-, and in d n─Бtham─Бn─Бс╕е. The verse (12 + 12: 11 + 12 = 47) is a
very irregular ‘"jagat─л."

Griffith

One form comes on, the other is reverted: to day and night the Strong One shapes and fits him. With humble prayer for aid we call on Surya, who knows the way, whose home is in the region.

  1. The earth-filling bull (mahiс╣г├б), track of the implorer, of
    undamaged sight, hath encompassed the all; beholding (sam-pa┼Ы) the

Mahiс╣гas is an evident intrusion, and the verse is strictly a

b─Бdham─Бnasya; for b, adbhutacakс╣гuс╣г pari saс╣Б babh┼лva; and, for

discoverable reason. тМКFive of SPP’s authorities (as well as W’s D.) read
babh┼лva without accent.тМЛ

Griffith

The suppliant’s way, filling the earth, the Mighty circleth the world with eye that none deceiveth. May he, all-seeing, well-disposed and holy, give ear and listen to the word I utter.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The greatness of him exceeds (p├бri) the earth, the ocean; shining
    abroad with light, it exceeds (p├бri) the sky, the atmosphere;
    beholding the all, beneficent, reverend, let him hear this which I say.
Notes

Ppp. again objects to our second half-verse, and gives instead:
ahor─Бtr─Бbhy─Бс╣Б saha saс╣Бvas─Бn─Б uс╣г─Б n─лyus pratar─Бd aviс╣гс╣нam. The
“jagat─л” is again a very rough one тМКas the Anukr. in part admitsтМЛ. тМКW.
interlines “encompasses” as an alternative to “exceeds."тМЛ

Griffith

Blazing with light his majesty hath compassed ocean and earth and heaven and air’s mid-region. May he, all-seeing, well-disposed and holy, give ear and listen to the word I utter.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Agni hath been awakened by the kindling of men to meet the dawn
    coming like a milch-cow; like young (yahv├б) [birds?] rising forth to
    a branch, the lights (bh─Бn├║) go forth unto the firmament (n─Б╠Бka).
Notes

Ppp. reads in d sasс╣Ыje. The verse is RV. v. 1. 1, and is found
also in other texts: SV. (i. 73; ii. 1096), VS. (xv. 24), TS. (iv. 4.
4┬╣), and MS. (ii. 13. 7), everywhere without a variant. тМКSV. (both
occurrences) reads sasrate in d; TS. accents ach├б at the end.тМЛ
It is quoted in V─Бit. 29. 8, apparently in connection with the verses
that follow it in RV. (iti tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubh─лс╕е).

тМКHere ends the second anuv─Бka, with 1 hymn and 46 verses. The quoted
Anukr. says с╣гaс╣н ┼Ыatv─Бriс╣Е┼Ыat.тМЛ

Griffith

Agni is weakened by the people’s fuel to meet the Dawn who cometh like a milch-cow, Like young trees shooting up on high their branches, his flames are mounting to the vault of heaven.

рдЕрдмреЛреСрдзрд┐ред рдЕреТрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГред рд╕реТрдореНрд╜рдЗрдзрд╛реСред рдЬрдирд╛реСрдирд╛рдореНред рдкреНрд░рддрд┐реСред рдзреЗреТрдиреБрдореНрд╜рдЗреСрд╡ред рдЖреТрд╜рдпреТрддреАрдореНред рдЙреТрд╖рд╕реСрдотАМреНред рдпреТрд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдГрд╜рдЗреСрд╡ред рдкреНрд░ред рд╡реТрдпрд╛рдореНред рдЙреТрддреНрд╜рдЬрд┐рд╣рд╛реСрдирд╛рдГред рдкреНрд░ред рднрд╛реТрдирд╡рдГреСред рд╕рд┐реТрд╕реНрд░реТрддреЗреТред рдирд╛рдХреСрдореНред рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреСред реи.рекремред

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ [рдЬреИрд╕реЗ] (рдЬрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдореЗрдВ (рд╕рдорд┐рдзрд╛) рдкреНрд░рдЬреНрд╡рд▓рд┐рдд рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рдзрди [рдХрд╛рд╖реНрда, рдШреГрдд, рдЕрдиреНрди рдЖрджрд┐] рд╕реЗ (рдЕрдмреЛрдзрд┐) рдЬрдЧрд╛рдпрд╛ рдЧрдпрд╛ рд╣реИ, [рдЕрдерд╡рд╛] (рдЗрд╡) рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рдЙрд╖рд╕рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐) рдЙрд╖рд╛ рд╕рдордп [рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрдГ рд╕рд╛рдпрдВ рд╕рдиреНрдзрд┐рд╡реЗрд▓рд╛] рдореЗрдВ (рдЖрдпрддреАрдореН) рдЖрддреА рд╣реБрдИ (рдзреЗрдиреБрдореН) рджреБрдзреИрд▓ рдЧреМ рдХреЛ [рд▓реЛрдЧ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ]ред [рдЕрдерд╡рд╛] (рдЗрд╡) рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рдЙрдЬреНрдЬрд┐рд╣рд╛рдирд╛рдГ) рдКрдБрдЪреЗ рдЪрд▓рддреЗ рд╣реБрдП (рдпрд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рдмрдбрд╝реЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ (рд╡рдпрд╛рдореН) рдЙрддреНрддрдо рдиреАрддрд┐ рдХреЛ (рдкреНрд░) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ [рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ], [рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА] (рднрд╛рдирд╡рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рди рд▓реЛрдЧ (рдирд╛рдХрдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк [рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛] рдХреЛ (рдЕрдЪреНрдЫ) рдЕрдЪреНрдЫреЗ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ (рдкреНрд░ рд╕рд┐рд╕реНрд░рддреЗ) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд░рд╣рддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ реерекремрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рднреЛрдЬреНрдп рдЕрдиреНрди рдЖрджрд┐ рд╕реЗ рдпрдерд╛рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐ рдЙрддреНрддреЗрдЬрд┐рдд рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдп рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдЧреМ рджреВрдз рдХреЗ рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рд┐рдп рд╣реЛрддреА рд╣реИ рдФрд░ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░рд╢реАрд▓реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЙрдЪрд┐рдд рдиреАрддрд┐ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рд╡реЗрджрд╡рд╛рдгреА рдкреНрд░рд┐рдп рд╣реЛрддреА рд╣реИ, рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА рд╕рдм рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рд╕рдорд░реНрде рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рд╕реБрдЦрд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдк рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛ рдХреЛ рдкрд╛рдХрд░ рдЖрдирдиреНрджрд┐рдд рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ реерекремреердпрд╣ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрдж рдореЗрдВ рд╣реИтИТрелредрезредрез, рдпрдЬреБрд░реНрд╡реЗрдж рдореЗрдВ резрелредреирек рдФрд░ рд╕рд╛рдорд╡реЗрдж рдореЗрдВтИТрдкреВреж резредреоредрезред рдФрд░ рдЙреж реоредрейредрезрей рее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: рекремтИТ(рдЕрдмреЛрдзрд┐) рдмреБрдзреНрдпрддреЗрд╕реНрдо (рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ) рд╢рд╛рд░реАрд░рд┐рдХрд╛рдЧреНрдирд┐рдГ (рд╕рдорд┐рдзрд╛) рдХрд╛рд╖реНрдард╛рдиреНрдирдШреГрддрд╛рджрд┐рдкреНрд░рджреАрдкрдирд╕рд╛рдзрдиреЗрди (рдЬрдирд╛рдирд╛рдореН) рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рдирд╛рдВ рдордзреНрдпреЗ (рдкреНрд░рддрд┐) (рдзреЗрдиреБрдореН) рджреАрдЧреНрдзреНрд░реАрдВ рдЧрд╛рдореН (рдЗрд╡) рдпрдерд╛ (рдЖрдпрддреАрдореН) рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреАрдореН (рдЙрд╖рд╕рдореН) рд╕рд╛рдВрд╣рд┐рддрд┐рдХреЛ рджреАрд░реНрдШрдГред рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрдГ рд╕рд╛рдпрдВ рд╕рдиреНрдзрд┐рд╡реЗрд▓рд╛рдореН (рдпрд╣реНрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╢реЗрд╡рд╛рдпрд╣реНрд╡рдЬрд┐рд╣реНрд╡рд╛режред рдЙреж резредрезрелрекред рдпрдЬ рджреЗрд╡рдкреВрдЬрд╛рджрд┐рд╖реБ-рд╡рдиреН, рдЬрд╕реНрдп рд╣рдГред рдпрд╣реНрд╡реЛ рдорд╣рдиреНрдирд╛рдо-рдирд┐рдШреж рейредрейред рдорд╣рд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдГ (рдкреНрд░) рдкреНрд░рдХрд░реНрд╖реЗрдг (рд╡рдпрд╛рдореН) рд╡рдп рдЧрддреМ-рдЕрдЪреН, рдЯрд╛рдкреНред рдЧрддрд┐рдореНред рдиреАрддрд┐рдореН (рдЙрдЬреНрдЬрд┐рд╣рд╛рдирд╛рдГ) рдУрд╣рд╛рдЩреН рдЧрддреМ-рд╢рд╛рдирдЪреНред рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддрдГ (рдкреНрд░) (рднрд╛рдирд╡рдГ) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдорд╛рдирд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рднрд╡рдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдГ (рд╕рд┐рд╕реНрд░рддреЗ) рд╕реГ рдЧрддреМ-рд▓рдЯреН, рд╢рдкрдГ рд╢реНрд▓реБрдГ, рдЖрддреНрдордиреЗрдкрджрдВ рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕рдореНред рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ (рдирд╛рдХрдореН) рд╕реБрдЦрд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрдВ рдкрд░рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдореН (рдЕрдЪреНрдЫ) рдЖрднрд┐рдореБрдЦреНрдпреЗрди рее
